<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Martin Brodeur</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>Martin Pierre Brodeur</b> (<small>French pronunciation: ​</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[maʁtɛ̃ bʁɔdœʁ]</a></span>; born May 6, 1972) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian" title="Canadian">Canadian</a>-<a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizen_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-citizen-1">[1]</a></sup> former <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> <a href="/wiki/Goaltender" title="Goaltender">goaltender</a> and the assistant general manager of the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Blues" title="St. Louis Blues">St. Louis Blues</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a> (NHL). In his 21-season tenure with the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Devils" title="New Jersey Devils">New Jersey Devils</a>, he won three <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> championships and five <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NHL)" title="Eastern Conference (NHL)">Eastern Conference</a> titles in 17 postseason campaigns. He also won two <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medal" title="Olympic medal">Olympic gold medals</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_national_men%27s_hockey_team" title="Canadian national men's hockey team">Team Canada</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010</a> <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a>, as well as several other medals with Team Canada in other international competitions. Brodeur is widely regarded as one of the greatest goaltenders of all time.</p>
<p>Brodeur holds numerous NHL and franchise records, including all-time regular season wins (691), losses (397), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shutout_(ice_hockey)" title="Shutout (ice hockey)">shutouts</a> (125), and games played (1,266).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> He won at least 30 games in twelve straight seasons between <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NHL_season" title="1995–96 NHL season">1995–96</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007-08_NHL_season" title="2007-08 NHL season">2007–08</a> and is the only goalie in NHL history with eight 40-win seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He is a four-time <a href="/wiki/Vezina_Trophy" title="Vezina Trophy">Vezina Trophy</a> winner, a five-time <a href="/wiki/William_M._Jennings_Trophy" title="William M. Jennings Trophy">Jennings Trophy</a> winner, a ten-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHL_All-Star_Game" title="NHL All-Star Game">NHL All-Star</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Calder_Memorial_Trophy" title="Calder Memorial Trophy">Calder Memorial Trophy</a> winner, and one of only two <a href="/wiki/List_of_goaltenders_who_have_scored_a_goal_in_an_NHL_game" title="List of goaltenders who have scored a goal in an NHL game">NHL goaltenders to score a goal</a> in both the regular season and the playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhl.com_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-nhl.com-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainBio_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-MainBio-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur used a <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_style#Profly_and_hybrid" title="Butterfly style">hybrid style</a> of goaltending by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stand-up_style" title="Stand-up style">standing up</a> more than <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_style" title="Butterfly style">butterfly style</a> goalies, though he adapted to more modern techniques at the latter stage of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cox_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-cox-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmasked_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-unmasked-8">[8]</a></sup> He was known for his puck handling, his positional play, and his reflexes, especially with his glove hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cox_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-cox-7">[7]</a></sup> Brodeur's prowess at puck handling was so well-known that it led in part to <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_rink#Goaltender_trapezoid" title="Ice hockey rink">the NHL changing its rules</a> regarding where goalies were allowed to handle the puck outside of the goal crease, adding what is known as "The Brodeur Rule".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamos2007_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diamos2007-9">[9]</a></sup> He announced his retirement in the middle of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_NHL_season" title="2014–15 NHL season">2014–15 season</a> after a brief stint with the Blues, having played in seven games with the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlayoffStats_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlayoffStats-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Martin Brodeur was born on May 6, 1972, in Montreal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> He was one of five children of <a href="/wiki/Denis_Brodeur" title="Denis Brodeur">Denis</a> and Mireille Brodeur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Denis played in the <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_1956_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 1956 Winter Olympics">1956 Olympics</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_national_men%27s_hockey_team" title="Canadian national men's hockey team">Team Canada</a> and won a bronze medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olympics_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOFjournal_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-HHOFjournal-14">[14]</a></sup> After his playing career, Denis was a longtime photographer for the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Canadiens" title="Montreal Canadiens">Montreal Canadiens</a>. For more than 20 years, he attended all Montreal games and practices, and when Martin was old enough, he came along. Brodeur idolized Canadiens goaltender <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Roy" title="Patrick Roy">Patrick Roy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur started playing hockey as a forward. His goaltending career began when his coach asked him if he wanted to play as a backup at the position in a youth tournament. Brodeur explained:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoalieDecision_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-GoalieDecision-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The next season my coach came up to me and said, 'Do you want to be a goalie or forward this year?' It was the biggest decision of my life, and I was seven years old. I don't know why I decided, but I thought it would be fun to play goal.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>When he was 12 years old, Brodeur briefly intended to stop playing hockey, after he had been removed from his team's lineup for not showing up at a game. Following a conversation with his brother Claude, though, he decided to continue playing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-always-17">[17]</a></sup> When receiving goaltending instructions in his teens, Brodeur was taught a variety of different styles, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_style" title="Butterfly style">butterfly</a> to stand-up, and paid attention to the technique of others playing the position. He attended a camp run by retired Soviet goalie <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Tretiak" title="Vladislav Tretiak">Vladislav Tretiak</a>, who encouraged the use of multiple methods; Brodeur believes that the concept made him "a student of the game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In the 1989–90 season, he made it to the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Major_Junior_Hockey_League" title="Quebec Major Junior Hockey League">Quebec Major Junior League</a>. While playing with the <a href="/wiki/Saint-Hyacinthe_Laser" title="Saint-Hyacinthe Laser">Saint-Hyacinthe Laser</a>, Brodeur made the QMJHL All-Rookie team in 1989–90 and the QMJHL 2nd All-Star Team in <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_QMJHL_season" title="1991–92 QMJHL season">1991–92</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOF_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-HHOF-19">[19]</a></sup> Brodeur was drafted by the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Devils" title="New Jersey Devils">New Jersey Devils</a> in the first round (20th overall) in the <a href="/wiki/1990_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="1990 NHL Entry Draft">1990 NHL Entry Draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOF_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-HHOF-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="NHL_career">NHL career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: NHL career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jersey_Devils">New Jersey Devils</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New Jersey Devils">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1991.E2.80.9395">1991–95</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1991–95">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_NHL_season" title="1991–92 NHL season">1991–92 NHL season</a>, Brodeur spent most of his time with the <a href="/wiki/Utica_Devils" title="Utica Devils">Utica Devils</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Hockey_League" title="American Hockey League">American Hockey League</a> (AHL), but was called up to the NHL on an emergency basis for four games when New Jersey goaltenders <a href="/wiki/Chris_Terreri" title="Chris Terreri">Chris Terreri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Billington" title="Craig Billington">Craig Billington</a> became injured. Brodeur won his NHL debut against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>, 4–2,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and played in one playoff game that season. Brodeur spent the following season in the AHL with Utica. However, in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NHL_season" title="1993–94 NHL season">1993–94 season</a>, Brodeur returned to the NHL permanently and gained recognition when he won the <a href="/wiki/Calder_Memorial_Trophy" title="Calder Memorial Trophy">Calder Trophy</a>, an annual award for the best rookie in the NHL. He led the Devils to the second-best record in the league and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1994_Stanley_Cup_Playoffs#Eastern_Conference_Final" title="1994 Stanley Cup Playoffs">Eastern Conference Finals</a> in the playoffs, where they lost to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">New York Rangers</a> in seven games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1994_Playoffs_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-1994_Playoffs-21">[21]</a></sup> He finished 2nd in <a href="/wiki/Goals_against_average" title="Goals against average">goals against average</a> (GAA) (2.40) and 4th in <a href="/wiki/Save_percentage" title="Save percentage">save percentage</a> (.915) in 47 games played during the regular season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> helping him eventually land the starting job over Terreri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NHL_season" title="1994–95 NHL season">1994–95 NHL season</a>, which was shortened to 48 games due to an <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NHL_lockout" title="1994–95 NHL lockout">extended lockout</a>, the Devils finished tied for 9th overall, 5th in their conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oral2_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-oral2-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> With the leadership of Brodeur, they defeated the Boston Bruins in the 1st round, shutting them out in three of their four wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oral2_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-oral2-24">[24]</a></sup> In the second round against the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Pittsburgh Penguins</a>, Brodeur gave up only nine goals and helped the Devils defeat the Penguins in five games. In the third round, the Devils defeated the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a> in six games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> giving them their first Stanley Cup Final appearance in franchise history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> against the heavily favoured <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Red_Wings" title="Detroit Red Wings">Detroit Red Wings</a>. The strong play of Brodeur and the Devils' "<a href="/wiki/Neutral_zone_trap" title="Neutral zone trap">trap</a>" method of defence made the series lopsided in favour of New Jersey, who swept the Red Wings 4 games to 0 while holding them to just seven goals in four games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Brodeur won a Stanley Cup in only his second full season in the NHL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> After the victory, he was quoted as saying:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainBio_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-MainBio-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In the last game against Detroit, the time from ten minutes left to one minute left was probably the longest nine minutes of my life. But from one to zero was probably the greatest time I've ever had. I didn't want the clock to run out. It was such a great feeling: people crying in the stands, people jumping up and down, people cheering. Guys couldn't even sit up on the bench. It was probably the best minute of my life.</p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1995.E2.80.9399">1995–99</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1995–99">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After a year of success, the Devils were in the middle of the pack for most of the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NHL_season" title="1995–96 NHL season">1995–96 season</a> and barely missed the playoffs. Brodeur played in 74 of his team's 82 games, setting a single-season record for most minutes played by a goalie, while having the 2nd-most shutouts (6) in the league. He was named the starter in the <a href="/wiki/46th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" title="46th National Hockey League All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Conference_(NHL)" title="Eastern Conference (NHL)">Eastern Conference</a> and stopped all 12 shots he faced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainBio_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-MainBio-5">[5]</a></sup> He finished fourth in voting for the <a href="/wiki/Vezina_Trophy" title="Vezina Trophy">Vezina Trophy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> which is awarded to the league's top goaltender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Brodeur also played on <a href="/wiki/Canada_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Canada men's national ice hockey team">Team Canada</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Cup_of_Hockey" title="1996 World Cup of Hockey">1996 World Cup of Hockey</a>, where Canada lost to the United States in the gold medal finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_NHL_season" title="1996–97 NHL season">1996–97 season</a>, the Devils finished 3rd in the NHL. Brodeur was runner-up for the Vezina Trophy, was named to the <a href="/wiki/47th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" title="47th National Hockey League All-Star Game">All-Star team</a>, and had the lowest goals against average by a goalie in almost 30 years, earning him the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jennings_Trophy" title="Jennings Trophy">Jennings Trophy</a>. He also had 10 shutouts and a .927 save percentage. On April 17, 1997, in the first game of a first-round playoff matchup against the Montreal Canadiens, Brodeur fired the puck the length of the ice and into the Canadiens' empty net to ensure a 5–2 victory. It was only the second time in NHL history that a <a href="/wiki/List_of_goaltenders_who_have_scored_a_goal_in_an_NHL_game" title="List of goaltenders who have scored a goal in an NHL game">goaltender had scored</a> in the playoffs, and the fifth time overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoalScored_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-GoalScored-34">[34]</a></sup> The Devils went on to win that series, but lost in the second round to the rival New York Rangers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following year, Brodeur had 43 wins and 10 shutouts in the regular season. The Devils finished first in the Eastern Conference,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1stplace1998_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-1stplace1998-37">[37]</a></sup> but lost in the first round of the playoffs to the eighth-seeded <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Senators" title="Ottawa Senators">Ottawa Senators</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98playoffs_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-98playoffs-38">[38]</a></sup> Once again, Brodeur made the <a href="/wiki/48th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" title="48th National Hockey League All-Star Game">All-Star Team</a>, finished as a runner-up for the Vezina Trophy, and won the Jennings Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98Jennings_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-98Jennings-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NHL_season" title="1998–99 NHL season">1998–99 season</a>, the Devils finished first in the Eastern Conference for the third straight year, with Brodeur winning 39 games. He was among the contenders for the Vezina Trophy and started in the <a href="/wiki/49th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" title="49th National Hockey League All-Star Game">All-Star game</a>, making his fourth appearance. However, the Devils lost in the first round to the Penguins. It was Brodeur's worst playoff performance to date statistically, as he allowed 20 goals in seven games with an .856 save percentage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlayoffStats_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-PlayoffStats-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1999.E2.80.932004">1999–2004</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1999–2004">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_NHL_season" title="1999–2000 NHL season">1999–2000 season</a>, on February 15, 2000, Brodeur was credited with his second career goal, as Brodeur was the last Devils player on the ice to touch the puck before <a href="/wiki/Daymond_Langkow" title="Daymond Langkow">Daymond Langkow</a> of the Flyers accidentally put the puck into his own empty net during a delayed penalty call against the Devils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2ndGoal_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-2ndGoal-40">[40]</a></sup> Brodeur had previously stopped an attempted Flyers shot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>That season, Brodeur won 43 games for the second time in his career, and the Devils finished with the fourth spot in the Eastern Conference after losing the division to the Flyers by two points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9900standings_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-9900standings-42">[42]</a></sup> Brodeur helped the Devils sweep the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panthers" title="Florida Panthers">Florida Panthers</a> in the first round, giving up only six goals in four games. In the next round against the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Maple_Leafs" title="Toronto Maple Leafs">Toronto Maple Leafs</a> he recorded two shutouts, including one in the final game of the series as the Devils went on to win four games to two, setting up a showdown with rival Philadelphia in the Eastern Conference Finals. The Flyers took a 3–1 series lead and had home ice to close out the series, but Brodeur gave up only one goal in each of the remaining three games of the series, propelling the Devils to a comeback series victory in 7 games. They went on to play the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Stars" title="Dallas Stars">Dallas Stars</a> in the Stanley Cup Final, who had a higher seed but fewer regular season points, giving the Devils home ice advantage in the series. After taking game one with a 7-goal rally against Dallas, the Devils were led by Brodeur the rest of the way as he gave up only six goals in the next five games, giving the team their second Stanley Cup Championship in six years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9900playoffs_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-9900playoffs-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next year, Brodeur topped the 40-win mark for the third time in his career, despite having an average GAA and save-percentage throughout the season. He played in the All-Star Game for the 6th consecutive season, and helped the Devils earn the top seed in the Eastern Conference. In the first round Brodeur recorded two shutouts against the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a> and the Devils took the series in six games. After struggling to beat 7th-seeded Toronto in seven games, the Devils defeated the 6th-seeded Penguins in the Eastern Conference Finals, where Brodeur added two more shutouts, both on the road. In their second straight Stanley Cup finals appearance, the Devils played a back-and-forth series against the top seeded <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Avalanche" title="Colorado Avalanche">Colorado Avalanche</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001finals1_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001finals1-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001finals2_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001finals2-45">[45]</a></sup> and lost in seven games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brodeur2003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="530" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Brodeur2003.jpg/220px-Brodeur2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Brodeur2003.jpg/330px-Brodeur2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Brodeur2003.jpg/440px-Brodeur2003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brodeur2003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brodeur during pre-game warmups in March 2003</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NHL_season" title="2001–02 NHL season">2001–02 season</a>, Brodeur finished among the league leaders in wins and GAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> Brodeur continued to lead the league in victories and remained a Vezina and MVP candidate. The next season, in <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_NHL_season" title="2002–03 NHL season">2002–03</a>, Brodeur won the Vezina Trophy for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vezina_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vezina-47">[47]</a></sup> He also won the Jennings Trophy again, was a <a href="/wiki/Hart_Memorial_Trophy" title="Hart Memorial Trophy">Hart Memorial Trophy</a> finalist for the league's Most Valuable Player, and was named a 1st Team All-Star and started in the All-Star Game. With one of the most impressive playoff performances of his career, Brodeur guided the Devils to their third Stanley Cup victory after seven-game series wins against the top-seeded Ottawa Senators and the 7th-seeded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mighty_Ducks_of_Anaheim" title="Mighty Ducks of Anaheim">Mighty Ducks of Anaheim</a>. He posted 3 shutouts against Anaheim and had a playoff total of 7 overall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> breaking the NHL record of 6 that had been set by <a href="/wiki/Dominik_Ha%C5%A1ek" title="Dominik Hašek">Dominik Hašek</a> the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Despite this, the <a href="/wiki/Conn_Smythe_Trophy" title="Conn Smythe Trophy">Conn Smythe Trophy</a> for playoff MVP was awarded to Anaheim goaltender <a href="/wiki/Jean-S%C3%A9bastien_Gigu%C3%A8re" title="Jean-Sébastien Giguère">Jean-Sébastien Giguère</a>, who became the first player not on the championship team to be named playoff MVP since <a href="/wiki/Ron_Hextall" title="Ron Hextall">Ron Hextall</a> of Philadelphia in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ConnSmythe_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ConnSmythe-50">[50]</a></sup> Some hockey writers speculated a New Jersey player did not win because there were multiple candidates, resulting in a <a href="/wiki/Split_vote" title="Split vote">split vote</a> among the sportswriters who selected the winner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PreSmythe03_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-PreSmythe03-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GiguereSmythe_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-GiguereSmythe-52">[52]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_NHL_season" title="2003–04 NHL season">2003–04 season</a>, Brodeur won his second consecutive Vezina Trophy and Jennings Trophy. He was a first Team All-Star,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> a starter in the NHL All-Star Game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> and a finalist for the Hart Trophy again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The Devils lost the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Division_(NHL)" title="Atlantic Division (NHL)">Atlantic Division</a> title by 1 point to the Philadelphia Flyers, who thus obtained the third seed and home ice advantage against the sixth-seeded Devils in the first round of the playoffs. This would be too much for Brodeur and the Devils to overcome, as the Flyers went on to defeat them in five games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Brodeur_Rule">The Brodeur Rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Brodeur Rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="647" data-file-width="392" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg/140px-NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg/210px-NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg/280px-NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg.png 2x" width="140"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NHL_Hockey_Rink.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The goaltender trapezoids behind each goal, added by the NHL before the 2005–06 season, were widely viewed as singling out Brodeur for his puck-handling skills.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the 2004–05 lockout and before the start of the 2005–06 season, the league instituted a new rule preventing goaltenders from playing the puck behind the <a href="/wiki/Goal_line_(ice_hockey)" title="Goal line (ice hockey)">goal line</a>, except within a <a href="/wiki/Trapezoid" title="Trapezoid">trapezoid</a>-shaped zone located behind the net. The trapezoid began at the goal line with angled lines six feet from each <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goal_post" title="Goal post">goal post</a> and widened to 28 feet at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boards_(ice_hockey)" title="Boards (ice hockey)">end boards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Former Flyers general manager Bobby Clarke was one of the leaders in getting the trapezoid implemented. This was viewed by many as singling out Brodeur, who was one of the best at getting behind the net to handle the puck, and has come to be known as the "Brodeur Rule".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamos2007_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Diamos2007-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the 2009 NHL General Managers' Meeting, it was discussed whether the rule should be eliminated as a solution to the increasing number of injuries on defenseman who were being hit hard by forechecking forwards. The forecheckers were no longer impeded by defencemen holding them up because of the crackdown on interference, which created situations where defencemen were being hit at high speeds. Brodeur believed that revoking the trapezoid could result in more scoring and more exciting games. He explained, "If you give the liberty to the goalies to play the puck, they'll mess up more than they're successful." He also expressed his concern for defencemen, "It's a no-brainer if they want to start to eliminate these huge hits for the defencemen... Whenever my defencemen or somebody was getting a big hit, I felt guilty that I let that guy get hit like that. Now, I've got to sit and watch all the time... You've got to try to find something because so many guys are getting hurt." At the time of his statement, Devils defencemen <a href="/wiki/Paul_Martin_(ice_hockey)" title="Paul Martin (ice hockey)">Paul Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Oduya" title="Johnny Oduya">Johnny Oduya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bryce_Salvador" title="Bryce Salvador">Bryce Salvador</a> were all out with injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brodeur_hopes_NHL_banishes_trapezoid_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brodeur_hopes_NHL_banishes_trapezoid-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ultimately the suggestion was rejected and the rule stayed in place. Former Maple Leafs GM <a href="/wiki/Brian_Burke_(ice_hockey)" title="Brian Burke (ice hockey)">Brian Burke</a> said, "We had originally approved a rule where the goaltenders couldn't handle the puck behind the net at all. The game was turning into a tennis match. You'd dump it in and the goalie would throw it out and now with the soft chip into the corner it turns into a puck battle and a forecheck opportunity, which is what we wanted."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHL_decides_to_keep_trapezoid_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHL_decides_to_keep_trapezoid-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.9309">2005–09</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2005–09">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_NHL_lockout" title="2004–05 NHL lockout">2004–05 NHL lockout</a> canceled the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_NHL_season" title="2004–05 NHL season">2004–05 season</a>, Brodeur signed a contract extension with the Devils on January 27, 2006, that would pay him $31.2 million over six years. In the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_NHL_season" title="2005–06 NHL season">2005–06 season</a> he posted 43 wins, adding onto his NHL records of what were now five 40-win seasons and ten consecutive 30-win seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30and10_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-30and10-60">[60]</a></sup> After struggling early in the season, his improved play later on made him a finalist for the Vezina Trophy for the third straight year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vezina0506_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vezina0506-61">[61]</a></sup> and helped lead the Devils to a surprising comeback in the last two months of the season that resulted in them winning the Atlantic Division in the final game of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlantic2006_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atlantic2006-62">[62]</a></sup> In the first round of the playoffs, he won a postseason series against the Rangers for the first time in his career, leading the Devils to a four-game sweep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> But a 4–1 series loss to the Carolina Hurricanes eliminated the Devils in the next round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006–07 season</a>, Brodeur made his ninth NHL All-Star Game appearance in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>, won his third Vezina Trophy and rose on several NHL records lists. On December 8, 2006, he posted a 2–0 victory over the Philadelphia Flyers for his 462nd career win, moving him into 2nd place on the all-time list ahead of <a href="/wiki/Ed_Belfour" title="Ed Belfour">Ed Belfour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Just a few weeks later, on December 26, Brodeur beat the Pittsburgh Penguins 3–0 to record his 85th career shutout, moving him past Glenn Hall for 3rd place on that all-time list and 1st place among all active goalies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> On February 1, 2007, Brodeur beat the Philadelphia Flyers 6–5 in overtime to take the all-time lead in overtime (non-shootout) wins with 45, passing Roy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The Devils' first 38 wins of the season were all with Brodeur in net, leading him to set a NHL record for most consecutive wins for a team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38consecutive_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-38consecutive-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1351" data-file-width="1815" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg/220px-Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg/330px-Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg/440px-Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_ready_vs_Capitals_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brodeur readies himself for action during a game in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 3, 2007, Brodeur tied the NHL record for most wins in a single season with 47, set by <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Parent" title="Bernie Parent">Bernie Parent</a> in <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_NHL_season" title="1973–74 NHL season">1973–74</a>, in a 2–1 shootout victory against the Ottawa Senators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Standings0226_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Standings0226-69">[69]</a></sup> Two days later, he broke the record with his 48th win in a 3–2 victory over the Philadelphia Flyers, which helped the Devils clinch the Atlantic Division title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Eastern Conference Quarterfinals against the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Lightning" title="Tampa Bay Lightning">Tampa Bay Lightning</a>, Brodeur started out shaky and the Devils fell behind two games to one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oust_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-oust-71">[71]</a></sup> He rebounded, however, to finish the series, and helped the team advance in six games, while passing <a href="/wiki/Grant_Fuhr" title="Grant Fuhr">Grant Fuhr</a> for second place in all-time playoff victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oust_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-oust-71">[71]</a></sup> In the second round against the Ottawa Senators, the Devils were defeated in five games as the Senators scored 15 goals during the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_NHL_season" title="2007–08 NHL season">2007–08 season</a>, Brodeur became the second goalie in NHL history to reach 500 wins with a victory against the Flyers on November 17, 2007. The only other goalie to achieve the feat is Roy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Brodeur was also named the starting goalie for the Eastern Conference in the <a href="/wiki/56th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" title="56th National Hockey League All-Star Game">2007–08 NHL All Star Game</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. However, he was unable to participate because of a family obligation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Averyrule.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="459" data-file-width="592" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Averyrule.jpg/220px-Averyrule.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Averyrule.jpg/330px-Averyrule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Averyrule.jpg/440px-Averyrule.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Averyrule.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sean Avery attempts to distract Brodeur during game 3 of the first round of the 2008 Stanley Cup Playoffs.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After losing a bitter series against the rival Rangers in the opening round of the 2008 NHL playoffs, Brodeur refused to shake <a href="/wiki/Sean_Avery" title="Sean Avery">Sean Avery</a>'s hand. During game three of the series, in an unusual move, Avery turned to face Brodeur during a 5-on-3 <a href="/wiki/Power_play_(sporting_term)" title="Power play (sporting term)">power play</a>, and began waving his hands and stick in front of Brodeur's face in an effort to distract him. The day after this game the NHL announced that it had revised its <a href="/wiki/Unsportsmanlike_conduct" title="Unsportsmanlike conduct">unsportsmanlike conduct</a> rule, now known as <a href="/wiki/Sean_Avery#The_Avery_Rule" title="Sean Avery">The Sean Avery Rule</a>, effectively outlawing such antics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur started wearing a new painted mask design for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NHL_season" title="2008–09 NHL season">2008–09 NHL season</a> with a stylized "MB30" on the front, replacing the "J" that had been on his mask for nearly his entire NHL career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> During a game on November 1, 2008, Brodeur suffered a "bruised elbow" which would later be diagnosed as a torn distal <a href="/wiki/Biceps" title="Biceps">biceps</a> tendon, the first major injury in his career. Following surgery on November 6, he would miss 16 weeks of the season before playing his next game on February 26, 2009. Upon returning from the injury, Brodeur registered a 4–0 shutout against the Colorado Avalanche for his 99th career shutout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Three days later, he recorded his 100th career shutout against the Philadelphia Flyers, three short of <a href="/wiki/Terry_Sawchuk" title="Terry Sawchuk">Terry Sawchuk</a>'s NHL record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9314">2009–14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2009–14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Beginning in 2009, Brodeur broke a number of career records for goaltenders. He missed 50 games in the 2008–09 season, but a winning streak upon his return pushed him near the NHL's all-time win record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-winningest_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-winningest-79">[79]</a></sup> On March 14, 2009, the Devils defeated the Canadiens 3–1 to give him the 551st win of his career, tying him with Roy for the NHL record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Three days later, Brodeur surpassed Roy with a 3–2 win over the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Blackhawks" title="Chicago Blackhawks">Chicago Blackhawks</a> in New Jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-winningest_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-winningest-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur topped another of Roy's previous marks on November 27, as he set the record for the most minutes played in the NHL, which had been 60,235.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> His 1,030th career appearance, which happened on December 18, broke Roy's record of 1,029.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> He also set the mark for the most regular-season shutouts with a 4–0 win against the Penguins on December 21, breaking Sawchuk's record of 103.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On December 30, 2009, Brodeur and the Devils shut out the Penguins, 2–0. It was his 105th career shutout, giving him the all-time professional record, surpassing <a href="/wiki/George_Hainsworth" title="George Hainsworth">George Hainsworth</a>'s total of 104 combined in the NHL (94) and <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada_Hockey_League" title="Western Canada Hockey League">Western Canada Hockey League</a> (10).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> On April 6, 2010, Brodeur reached his 600th career win by defeating the Thrashers 3–0. This was also his 110th career shutout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1049" data-file-width="1461" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg/220px-Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg/330px-Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg/440px-Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_vs_Islanders_in_Nov_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brodeur playing in November 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10 NHL season</a>, Brodeur led the NHL in wins (45), shutouts (9), games played (77) and minutes played (4,499). He also won his fifth Jennings Trophy and had the third-best GAA in the league, leading his team to back-to-back division wins that included a 6–0 regular-season sweep of the defending Stanley Cup champion Penguins. However, the Devils lost in the first round of the playoffs, losing to the seventh-seeded Flyers in five games. Brodeur had a 5–18–1 stretch to begin the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> as New Jersey slumped to the bottom of the NHL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Although the Devils improved in the second half of the season, they did not reach the <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_playoffs" title="2011 Stanley Cup playoffs">playoffs</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-back_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-back-89">[89]</a></sup> Brodeur recorded 23 wins and a 2.45 GAA,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> but had his lowest save percentage (.903) in 16 seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-back_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-back-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Devils returned to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Stanley_Cup_playoffs" title="2012 Stanley Cup playoffs">playoffs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season" title="2011–12 NHL season">2011–12 NHL season</a>, as Brodeur recorded his 14th 30-win <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_New_Jersey_Devils_season" title="2011–12 New Jersey Devils season">season</a>. In Game 1 of the conference quarterfinals against the Panthers, Brodeur became only the second goaltender to record 100 playoff wins in a 3–2 Devils victory. In Game 4 with a 4–0 victory, Brodeur broke the NHL career playoff shutout record with his 24th, surpassing Roy, who had 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The Devils advanced by winning Game 7 in double overtime, after Brodeur had made 43 saves to keep his team in the contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-last-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a second round series win over the Flyers, Brodeur and the Devils defeated the Rangers four games to two in the Eastern Conference finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-last-91">[91]</a></sup> New Jersey won the sixth game 3–2 on an overtime goal by <a href="/wiki/Adam_Henrique" title="Adam Henrique">Adam Henrique</a>, leading to Brodeur's fifth Stanley Cup Finals appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The Devils lost in the Finals to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings" title="Los Angeles Kings">Los Angeles Kings</a> in six games. Brodeur was 14–10 in the postseason with a save percentage of .917, after winning 16 playoff games in the previous eight years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-last_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-last-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the off-season of 2012, Brodeur hired agent <a href="/wiki/Pat_Brisson" title="Pat Brisson">Pat Brisson</a>, leading many analysts to believe he would test free-agency or retire. However, on July 2, 2012, Brodeur agreed to a two-year, $9 million deal to remain with the Devils, alongside backup goalie <a href="/wiki/Johan_Hedberg" title="Johan Hedberg">Johan Hedberg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On March 21, 2013, in his first game back from a month-long absence due to a pinched nerve injury in his upper back, Brodeur was credited with a power play goal against the Carolina Hurricanes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scores_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-scores-94">[94]</a></sup> making him the only NHL goalie to record three career goals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> and the first goalie to score on the power play since <a href="/wiki/Evgeni_Nabokov" title="Evgeni Nabokov">Evgeni Nabokov</a> in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scores_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-scores-94">[94]</a></sup> Brodeur had a 13–9–7 record in his 29 appearance in 2012–13, with a 2.22 GAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> The following season, he shared the Devils' starting goalie position with <a href="/wiki/Cory_Schneider" title="Cory Schneider">Cory Schneider</a>, whose 45 games played were six more than Brodeur's total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exits_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-exits-96">[96]</a></sup> Brodeur's statistical performance declined, as his GAA increased to 2.51, more than half a goal higher than Schneider. In 39 games played, Brodeur had a .901 save percentage, lower than the league average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-test-97">[97]</a></sup> Among his 19 wins in 2013–14 was a victory in the season finale against Boston, his 688th for New Jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-exits_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-exits-96">[96]</a></sup> On June 6, 2014, Brodeur told ESPN he would test the free agency market for the 2014–15 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-test-97">[97]</a></sup> and his 21-year tenure with the Devils ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Louis_Blues">St. Louis Blues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: St. Louis Blues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 26, 2014 Brodeur signed a tryout contract with the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Blues" title="St. Louis Blues">St. Louis Blues</a> after their starting netminder, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Elliott" title="Brian Elliott">Brian Elliott</a>, was injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> A week later, on December 2, Brodeur signed a one-year, $700,000 deal with the Blues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 27, 2015, it was reported that Brodeur had decided to retire from the NHL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-always-17">[17]</a></sup> The decision followed Elliott's return to the Blues, as Brodeur had been demoted to the team's number three goalie behind Elliott and <a href="/wiki/Jake_Allen_(ice_hockey)" title="Jake Allen (ice hockey)">Jake Allen</a>. Brodeur announced the news at a press conference two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retires_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-retires-101">[101]</a></sup> He retired having started just five games with the Blues, going 3–3–0 in seven appearances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-hr-22">[22]</a></sup> His final NHL win was a 3–0 shutout against the Avalanche on December 29, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retires_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-retires-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-NHL_career">Post-NHL career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Post-NHL career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Upon announcing his retirement, Brodeur was hired by the Blues as a special assistant to GM Doug Armstrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retires_101-2"><a href="#cite_note-retires-101">[101]</a></sup> On May 22, 2015, Armstrong announced that Brodeur and the Blues had agreed to a three-year contract naming Brodeur as an assistant general manager of the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 8, 2016, the New Jersey Devils unveiled a bronze statue of Brodeur which will be displayed outside the Prudential Center. The statue was formally dedicated on October 22, 2016 in a ceremony before the game against the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Wild" title="Minnesota Wild">Minnesota Wild</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The following evening, February 9, 2016, Brodeur's No. 30 jersey was retired by the Devils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_play">International play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: International play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="Gold medal – first place" data-file-height="16" data-file-width="16" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg/16px-Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg/24px-Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg/32px-Gold_medal_icon_%28G_initial%29.svg.png 2x" title="Gold medal – first place" width="16"/></td>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="Silver medal – second place" data-file-height="16" data-file-width="16" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/16px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/24px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/32px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 2x" title="Silver medal – second place" width="16"/></td>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="Silver medal – second place" data-file-height="16" data-file-width="16" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/16px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/24px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/32px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 2x" title="Silver medal – second place" width="16"/></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2005_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="2005 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2005 Austria</a></span></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Brodeur was selected as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_men%27s_national_hockey_team" title="Canada men's national hockey team">Team Canada</a>'s back-up goalie to Roy for the <a href="/wiki/1998_Winter_Olympics" title="1998 Winter Olympics">1998 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nagano,_Nagano" title="Nagano, Nagano">Nagano</a>, Japan, but did not get to play. Canada failed to win a medal after losing the bronze-medal match to <a href="/wiki/Finland_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Finland men's national ice hockey team">Finland</a>, a game in which many people thought Brodeur should have played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NoBronze_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-NoBronze-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympic_Games/Ice_hockey" title="2002 Winter Olympic Games/Ice hockey">2002 Olympics</a> at <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, Brodeur was initially named the backup behind <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Joseph" title="Curtis Joseph">Curtis Joseph</a>. But following Joseph's losing the tournament opener against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Sweden men's national ice hockey team">Sweden</a>, Brodeur was named the starting goaltender the rest of the way, and won gold for Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-change_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-change-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> He went undefeated in the tournament, stopping 31 of 33 shots in the gold-medal victory over <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="United States men's national ice hockey team">Team USA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur then led Team Canada to a <a href="/wiki/World_Cup_of_Hockey" title="World Cup of Hockey">World Cup of Hockey</a> championship in 2004, allowing only 5 goals in five games. He led all goalies in GAA and save percentage while going undefeated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-better_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-better-110">[110]</a></sup> He had another impressive performance for the team at the world hockey championships in the following year. After this, <i>The Sports Forecaster 2005–06</i> said the following:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainBio_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-MainBio-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Brodeur is arguably the top goaltender in the world. Fresh off a World Cup win in 2004 and another strong performance at the 2005 IIHF World hockey championships. He's the game's best puck-handling goaltender, though the NHL's new rules changes may somewhat alter that effectiveness.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Brodeur was selected as Team Canada's starter in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> He started in 4 games, but Canada failed to win a medal after losing to <a href="/wiki/Russia_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Russia men's national ice hockey team">Russia</a> in the quarterfinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was one of the three goalies on Team Canada for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-change_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-change-107">[107]</a></sup> He registered a shootout win against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Switzerland men's national ice hockey team">Switzerland</a> and a loss to the United States. After the loss to the US, he was benched for the remainder of the 2010 Games in favour of <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Luongo" title="Roberto Luongo">Roberto Luongo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur was selected to represent Canada in:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1996_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="1996 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">1996 IIHF World Championships</a> (<b>silver</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1996_World_Cup_of_Hockey" title="1996 World Cup of Hockey">1996 World Cup of Hockey</a> (<b>silver</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_1998_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 1998 Winter Olympics">1998 Winter Olympic Games</a> (4th place)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympic Games</a> (<b>gold</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-3"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2004_World_Cup_of_Hockey" title="2004 World Cup of Hockey">2004 World Cup of Hockey</a> (<b>champion</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-better_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-better-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2005_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="2005 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2005 IIHF World Championships</a> (<b>silver</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-4"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_2006_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a> (lost quarterfinal)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> (<b>gold</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sr_109-5"><a href="#cite_note-sr-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_2012.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="611" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Martin_Brodeur_2012.png/170px-Martin_Brodeur_2012.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Martin_Brodeur_2012.png/255px-Martin_Brodeur_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Martin_Brodeur_2012.png/340px-Martin_Brodeur_2012.png 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Brodeur_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Martin Brodeur before a game in Calgary during the 2011–2012 season</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brodeur married Melanie Dubois (a native of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Liboire,_Quebec" title="Saint-Liboire, Quebec">Saint-Liboire, Quebec</a>) in August 1995 and has four children:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOFjournal_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-HHOFjournal-14">[14]</a></sup> Anthony, born in 1995; twin sons, William and Jeremy, born in 1996; and Annabelle Antoinette, born in 2002. Melanie filed for divorce during the 2003 playoffs amid reports that Brodeur was having an affair with Genevieve Nault, the wife of Melanie's brother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divorce_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-divorce-114">[114]</a></sup> The incident was referred to by opposing fans during the playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heckling_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-heckling-115">[115]</a></sup> The reports proved to be true, as he and Genevieve married in June 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Their first child together, Maxime Philippe Brodeur, was born in November 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur is regarded as an engaging <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raconteur" title="Raconteur">raconteur</a> in his spare time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOFjournal_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-HHOFjournal-14">[14]</a></sup> He has hosted a <a href="/wiki/Street_hockey" title="Street hockey">street hockey</a> tournament in his hometown of St. Leonard, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, for each of the Devils' <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> championships, where he played as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forward_(hockey)" title="Forward (hockey)">forward</a>. His oldest brother, Denis Jr., is a photographer like their father, and his other older brother, Claude, was a minor league baseball pitcher in the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>' organization. He has two sisters, Line and Sylvie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HHOFjournal_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-HHOFjournal-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Brodeur began co-authoring his autobiography, <i>Brodeur: Beyond the Crease</i>, with long-time <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Star" title="Toronto Star">Toronto Star</a></i> columnist and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> contributor <a href="/wiki/Damien_Cox" title="Damien Cox">Damien Cox</a>, which was released in October 2006. Some of the things Brodeur talks about in the book are player salaries and contracts, NHL marketing, <a href="/wiki/Lou_Lamoriello" title="Lou Lamoriello">Lou Lamoriello</a>, and the Devils' new arena in Newark, the <a href="/wiki/Prudential_Center" title="Prudential Center">Prudential Center</a>. Brodeur also includes his views on the "new NHL" after the lockout, and how it affected his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-biography-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur co-owns a business called La Pizzeria Etc. with former teammate <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Souray" title="Sheldon Souray">Sheldon Souray</a>. The idea came about after Souray was traded to play in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, the city in which the business now operates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pizzeria_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pizzeria-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur was a resident of <a href="/wiki/North_Caldwell,_New_Jersey" title="North Caldwell, New Jersey">North Caldwell, New Jersey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> and currently resides in <a href="/wiki/West_Orange,_New_Jersey" title="West Orange, New Jersey">West Orange, New Jersey</a>, near the Devils' former practice facility, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Mountain_Arena" title="South Mountain Arena">South Mountain Arena</a>. He became a naturalized United States citizen on December 1, 2009, but per IIHF rules would only be able to compete for Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citizen_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-citizen-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 30, 2013, the Devils traded for the 208th pick in the <a href="/wiki/2013_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="2013 NHL Entry Draft">2013 NHL Entry Draft</a> and Brodeur was asked to make the announcement to select his son, Anthony. In August 2015, Anthony signed with the <a href="/wiki/Penticton_Vees" title="Penticton Vees">Penticton Vees</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Hockey_League" title="British Columbia Hockey League">British Columbia Hockey League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fans picked Brodeur to appear on the cover of the video game <a href="/wiki/NHL_14" title="NHL 14">NHL 14</a>, choosing him in a series of votes that included 60 players. He was the first goalie in 17 years to have his image on the cover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Bolded numbers</b> indicate league leader.</p>
<p><i><b>Italicized numbers</b></i> indicate NHL records.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Brodeur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During his NHL career, Brodeur set numerous league records. He ended his career with 691 wins, 140 more than Roy, who is second on the NHL's all-time list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Brodeur extended his record shutout total to 125, 22 more than second-place Sawchuk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> After his final season, he had played in 1,266 regular season games, a total more than 200 above that of any other goalie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In nine seasons, Brodeur was the NHL wins leader, and in five other seasons he was among the top five goalies in the category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Brodeur's honors include three Vezina Trophy wins as the top goalie in the NHL, and the 1993–94 Calder Trophy as rookie of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-best-127">[127]</a></sup> His total of five Jennings Trophies is tied for the most in NHL history, matching Roy's record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In postseason play, he had the most shutouts of any NHL goalie (24), and his 113 playoff wins ranks second all-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sportswriters and players have called Brodeur one of the greatest goalies in NHL history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-always-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-best-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debate_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-debate-130">[130]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>'</i>s Kevin Allen placed Brodeur in a group including Roy and Sawchuk as the leading NHL goalie, noting that Brodeur had the advantage in wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-always_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-always-17">[17]</a></sup> Writer Steve Politi noted Brodeur's longevity as an advantage on other top all-time goalies such as Roy; Brodeur played 70 or more games in 12 seasons, compared to 0 for Roy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debate_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-debate-130">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet" title="Sportsnet">Sportsnet</a>'s Chris Boyle, after running a statistical analysis, placed Broduer eighth in his all-time goaltending list; he offered the rationale that Brodeur's teammates helped him achieve his major records, while goalies such as Roy and Hašek had superior stats in their best seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brodeur is remembered for his playing style: writer Katie Strang called him "one of the most innovative [goalies] ever to play the game", due to his "superior puck-handling skills".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Gomez" title="Scott Gomez">Scott Gomez</a>, a former teammate of Brodeur in New Jersey, considered his goalie to be the equivalent of an extra defenceman. The Brodeur Rule, which his play helped inspire the league to institute starting in the 2005–06 season, remains in place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_127-2"><a href="#cite_note-best-127">[127]</a></sup> His playing style proved uncommon among goalies of his era, as most of his competitors used a butterfly style exclusively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmasked_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-unmasked-8">[8]</a></sup> Brodeur is considered a likely candidate for induction into the <a href="/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame" title="Hockey Hall of Fame">Hockey Hall of Fame</a> once he becomes eligible to appear on the ballot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_127-3"><a href="#cite_note-best-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
